## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the core ODE formulation in population ecology. The growth rate typically depends on P through density-dependent mechanisms and may depend on t through environmental variation.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (logistic with periodic environmental forcing)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting)
- Weak Allee logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (weak Allee effect)
- Delayed density dependence proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (time as proxy for lagged effects)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP/dt is proportional to P at low densities, the per-capita growth rate r(P) = dP_dt/P is the key quantity to analyze for density dependence
- A sign change in dP/dt at specific P values indicates equilibrium points (carrying capacity or Allee threshold) → look for polynomial roots in P
- If dP/dt/P decreases linearly with P, the system is classic logistic → dP_dt = c0*P + c1*P^2
- Periodic or oscillatory residuals in time suggest seasonal forcing → multiplicative sinusoidal modulation (1 + c*sin(c*t))
- If dP/dt = 0 at both P = 0 and a nonzero P, the simplest structure is P*(K-P) form with factored roots
- Concave-down dP/dt vs P relationship (hump-shaped) is the hallmark of logistic-family models
- If per-capita growth rate dP_dt/P shows a non-monotonic relationship with P (initially increasing then decreasing), Allee effects are present
- Asymmetric growth curves (faster approach to carrying capacity from below vs above) suggest Gompertz or Richards models rather than symmetric logistic

I need to first simplify the GT expression to understand its structure.

**GT numerical expression:**
```
0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333
```

Let me expand this. Let me denote a = 0.72136, b = 6.6511, d = 13.538.

**First term:** a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P
= a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P
= a*[P/b - P²/(bd) - 1 + P/d]*P
= a*[P²/b - P³/(bd) - P + P²/d]

**Second term:** a*(1 - P/d)*P
= a*[P - P²/d]

**Third term:** a*P^(1/3)

**Combining all terms:**
- P³ term: -a/(bd) = -0.72136/(6.6511 × 13.538) = -0.72136/90.0596 ≈ -0.008010
- P² term: a/b + a/d - a/d = a/b = 0.72136/6.6511 ≈ 0.10846
- P term: -a + a = 0
- P^(1/3) term: a ≈ 0.72136

So the GT simplifies to:
**GT = c₁·P³ + c₂·P² + c₀·P^(1/3)**

where c₁ ≈ -0.008010, c₂ ≈ 0.10846, c₀ ≈ 0.72136.

This is a function of P only (no t dependence), with three terms: P^(1/3), P², P³.

Now I check candidates that can match this form: **c0·P^(1/3) + c1·P³ + c2·P²**

**Candidate 42:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2`

This is exactly P^(1/3)·c0 + P³·c1 + P²·c2. Setting c0 = 0.72136, c1 = -0.008010, c2 = 0.10846 gives the GT exactly.

**This matches!**

Let me verify there are no other matches worth noting, but candidate 42 is a clear match.

I need to first simplify the Ground Truth expression to understand what functional form it takes.

**GT expression:**
```
0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P^(1/3)
```

Let me denote `a = 0.7213553457664288`, `b = 6.6511035054181695`, `d = 13.538092585698905`.

**First term:** `a*(-1 + P/b)*(1 - P/d)*P`
= `a*(P/b - 1)*(1 - P/d)*P`

**Second term:** `a*(1 - P/d)*P`

Let me combine the first two terms. Factor out `a*(1 - P/d)*P`:
= `a*(1 - P/d)*P * [(-1 + P/b) + 1]`
= `a*(1 - P/d)*P * (P/b)`
= `a*P²/b * (1 - P/d)`
= `a*P²/b - a*P³/(b*d)`

**Third term:** `a*P^(1/3)`

So the GT simplifies to:
```
GT = a*P^(1/3) + (a/b)*P² - (a/(b*d))*P³
```

Computing constants:
- Coefficient of P^(1/3): `a ≈ 0.72136`
- Coefficient of P²: `a/b ≈ 0.72136/6.6511 ≈ 0.10845`
- Coefficient of P³: `-a/(b*d) ≈ -0.72136/90.08 ≈ -0.008008`

So **GT = c₀*P^(1/3) + c₁*P³ + c₂*P²** where c₀ ≈ 0.72136, c₁ ≈ -0.008008, c₂ ≈ 0.10845.

This is exactly the form: **P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2**

Now I'll check each candidate against this. The GT has no dependence on `t`, no constant term, and only three basis functions: P^(1/3), P², P³.

For each candidate, I need to check if extra terms can be zeroed out (by setting constants to 0) and if the remaining terms match.

Let me go through systematically:

- **Candidate 1:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5)` — Set c3=0 → matches GT. **MATCH**

- **Candidate 2:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P³*c1 + P²*c2 + c3 + c4*sin(c5 + c6*t)` — Set c3=0, c4=0 → matches. **MATCH**
